1. Kim Jong-un is one of my Facebook friends.
2. I couldn’t believe it. [audience laughing] He’s always liking my stuff. “Hey, I like that.” Thanks, Kim Jong-un.
3. I read recently, absolute truth, they said Kim Jong-un is considering outlawing sarcasm in North Korea.
4. Wow.
5. I wonder if he proposed that and one of his generals said, “Oh, yeah.
6. That’ll work.” END OF JOKE.

Let's analyze each line:

1. **"Kim Jong-un is one of my Facebook friends."**
   - This line sets up the initial context of the joke by introducing an unexpected and absurd scenario (Kim Jong-un being a Facebook friend).
   - **Label:** establishing context

2. **"I couldn’t believe it. [audience laughing] He’s always liking my stuff. “Hey, I like that.” Thanks, Kim Jong-un."**
   - This line builds on the context by adding more absurdity and humor through the speaker's reaction and the imagined interaction with Kim Jong-un.
   - **Label:** escalation

3. **"I read recently, absolute truth, they said Kim Jong-un is considering outlawing sarcasm in North Korea."**
   - This line introduces a new piece of information that seems to follow from the previous absurdity but also introduces a real-world element that's inherently funny.
   - **Label:** setup

4. **"Wow."**
   - This is a reaction to the previous line, expressing surprise or disbelief, which adds to the humor.
   - **Label:** timing

5. **"I wonder if he proposed that and one of his generals said, “Oh, yeah."**
   - This line is a hypothetical scenario that builds on the previous line, adding a layer of absurdity and humor.
   - **Label:** escalation

6. **"That’ll work.” END OF JOKE."**
   - This line completes the hypothetical scenario and serves as the punchline of the joke, delivering the final humorous twist.
   - **Label:** punchline

Now, I'll format the final answer as specified.

=== Prompt 49 ===

Please use the following definitions: establishing context: introduces the situation, characters, or setting. setup: introduces a premise or question that will later be resolved or subverted. escalation: increases the tension or humor by building upon the setup. subversion: introduces an unexpected twist or reversal. callback: references an earlier joke or setup for comedic effect. misdirection: leads the audience to expect one thing but delivers another. timing: relies on the timing of delivery for comedic effect. meta-humor: humor that comments on the nature of humor or the joke itself. punchline: the line that delivers the joke's resolution or climax. redirection: shifts focus away from the current topic to another. non-line: a sound effect or other non-verbal element. wrap-up: concludes the joke or ties up loose ends. repetition: repeats a phrase or concept for comedic effect. Okay, let's start by breaking down the joke line by line and see what each part is doing.

1. **"So, I was driving today, and I came upon a truck… Pulling a horse trailer with a sign on the back– “caution: transporting show horses.”"**  
   This sets up the initial scenario. The speaker is driving and sees a truck with a specific type of trailer. This is **establishing context**.

2. **"Ohh. “Oh, 10:00 and 2:00! “We’re sharin’ the road with show horses."**  
   The speaker is reacting to the sign, which introduces the situation. This is the **setup** for the joke, explaining the scenario.

3. **"If I start to lose control, I’ll hit one of these cars with people! “Or at least a trailer with just plain old horses.\nBut those horses, they gotta put on a show!”**  
   Here, the speaker is escalating the problem by imagining the consequences of a crash. The contrast between "plain old horses" and "show horses" adds tension. This is **escalation**.

4. **"What are you supposed to do in a spin-out?\nDon’t hit the show horses!\nAnything but the show horses!\nCan you imagine hitting– [gibberish]"**  
   This is the **punchline**. It delivers the humorous advice to avoid hitting the show horses, emphasizing their importance in a funny way.

5. **"then I came up on another truck pulling a trailer with a sign on the back, “don’t worry, just dumb old donkeys.”"**  
   Introducing a new scenario with donkeys after the horses. This is a **callback** to the previous setup but changes the context for a twist.

6. **"I was crossing over the line.\nBoom, boom.\nBoom.\nHee-haw!\nBoom.\nWho cares?\nJust dumb old donkeys.\nThey refuse to apply themselves.[Brays]heck with them.\nThose dumb old donkeys."**  
   This part uses **misdirection** and **redirection**. The speaker shifts focus from the tense scenario with horses to the donkeys, which are portrayed as unimportant and silly. The onomatopoeia and dismissive tone contrast with the earlier seriousness.

7. **"END OF JOKE."**  
   This is the **wrap-up**, signaling the end of the joke.

Now, let's assign labels to each line based on their roles in the joke structure.

   - This line introduces the main issue or context of the joke.
   - **Label:** *establishing context*

2. **"I feel bad—my poor father took me aside."**  
   - Introduces a specific scenario where the pressure is coming from the father, setting up the first part of the joke.
   - **Label:** *setup*

3. **"He said, 'You know, your mother and I really want grandkids.'"**  
   - Adds more detail to the scenario, building on the setup.
   - **Label:** *setup*

4. **"And I said, 'Well, then you’d better get cracking!'"**  
   - A humorous response to the father's comment, introducing a twist.
   - **Label:** *subversion*

   - **Label:** *escalation*

   - Intensifies the situation, showing the escalation of the pressure from the family.
   - **Label:** *escalation*

7. **"That’s when it hit me—they think I’m going to take care of them!"**  
   - The punchline of the joke, where the twist is revealed and the humor is realized.
   - **Label:** *punchline*

=== Prompt 114 ===
 To get full credit, you must label each line correctly. Here are some definitions to guide you:establishing context: sets up the context for the joke (e.g., where it takes place, who is involved).setup: sets up a premise or situation that will lead to a punchline.escalation: increases the tension or stakes in the joke, building toward a punchline.subversion: introduces an unexpected twist that contradicts the audience’s expectations.callback: references a previous joke or element to create continuity or reinforce a theme.misdirection: leads the audience away from the actual punchline.timing: refers to the rhythm or pacing of the joke, often through pauses or line breaks.meta-humor: humor that is self-aware or comments on the nature of humor itself.punchline: the line that delivers the joke’s humorous conclusion.redirection: shifts the focus of the joke in a new direction, often leading to a punchline.non-line: a line that is not part of the joke structure (e.g., dialogue tags, actions).wrap-up: concludes the joke, often with a final punchline or reflection.repetition: repeats a phrase or idea for comedic effect.

1. **"…so then I’m trying to outsilly Oona, you know."**

   - **Label: setup**

3. **"I go, 'What does the penguin say to her parents when she’s hungry?'"**  
   - This is the beginning of the joke setup, leading up to the punchline.  
   - **Label: setup**

4. **"And she says, 'What?'"**  
   - This line shows the reaction of the listener, adding to the dialogue and building up the interaction.  
   - **Label: timing**

5. **"And I say, 'Waddle we have for dinner?'"**

   - **Label: punchline**

6. **"And… Don’t feel like you have to laugh at that. END OF JOKE."**
